< Review>
Expect a long wait time, even with appointment. They're nice, they do good work and they do it fast. Five star work, minus a star for hour+ wait time. We went on a Wednesday afternoon.

2 weeks later update: his is my second experience. My first one went great. I have no complaints aside from the wait time with an appointment ~ hour. My nails turned out exactly how I wanted them.

This second time evens the score to 3 stars. It was very clear my nail technician was uncomfortable doing my dip nails with added tip. There was a lot of other-language and gesturing, people stopping by while I was being worked on to check and another technician that translated near me peeked over occasionally. Let me add that the nails look fine if a little wobbly. Now the cons:

1. In sanding down my nails after initial removal - the technician literally buffed into my cuticles. I bled. It's still sore. As it went on there were a couple of times the sander got painfully close but no blood.
2. The incident was addressed with a couple sincere "sorry"'s but it wasn't cleaned or dabbed or anything. The entire procedure continued. Dip stung. Burned the whole time.
3. I got almond/stiletto shapes and when they used the scissors to trim down they sometimes pushed the scissors too close and was "cutting" into my finger. I politely told them when I feared they'd actually cut through to my flesh.

When I pointed out that it wasn't coming off after I washed my hands repeatedly and one other technician assuring me soap and rubbing would remove it (It didn't) another nice technician brought me a cotton ball with acetone on it.
5. My fake nail - to real nail glue application glued my real - nail to my real - finger/bed.

So overall they look fine, but at what cost?

One great experience (with Jerry, will book with him) and one bad. Three stars.<//Review>

<rating>5<//rating><text>Delectable Indonesian food!!

Came here for dinner on a Friday night and it wasn't too busy. The restaurant is located at the corner of a big building complex and theirs plenty of non meter street parking.

The place is not too big with only a couple of tables for groups of four and the menu is pretty simple too. Since Im not too familiar with Indonesian food I was super excited to try anything! The sate dishes looked really good so I definitely wanted that and they also had soups and appetizers.

I went with one of their combo dinners since it included a little bit of everything from the menu. I got combo #3 and it came with three sate squewers and soup. My bf also got combo #3 and we shared their peanut sauce salad.

The salad came out first and it was amazing!! It was covered in a peanut sauce and it had shrimp chips. They had a very good house spicy sauce that I wanted them to bottle for me to take home!! It was so good!! I love spicy and this sauce had a great kick!!

The sate came out next and I lost it! It was so good!! I got two sate of beef and one of potato. The beef had a line of peanut sauce OMG!!  My coconut broth beef soup was also very flavorful and very tasty. My bf and I devoured our delicious food and we're very happy we found this place!! We will definitely make the trip out again to dine here! So worth it!!<//text><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNPFXK0XKIfKXBVupdwDPl2k62Qy8iRU8DJNpJV=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNKxYXLIvXCW6nb5xaBld3NA1G6gsegsIXLIwOB=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPPuHAd3a5YcvuQ2DkFXNofeF9Pdvdsln0mLIUd=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPmtDVzv4ZbOJxTHd9B-b9oWqPsm-euoQKdlB68=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN_p2TDRDTvxNKaJGkdfjsvWM1Jemijxaijn7Ka=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN0QPVe54iq7zkLzov3eSHj5ubDpNQtPDxId-p3=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipP8SWY0AwVTT8URfNzGW_QGS9fT0FAI8laUXRhe=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPv3OzgvaGzhZOVEDNXE3RkZTUu5SKxtABRiFDx=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPaMi11yKXCQ-RmB4gA9VB77G-OxjmGVonmhOYS=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//Pics><Response>None</Response>< gmapID>

<Rate>4< /Rate>< Text>
First visit on a weeknight before 8p. Not crowded so service wasn't slow. I started with some a la carte items such as the Gado Gado salad (cooked vegetables with peanut sauce and shrimp crackers) and the corn fritters. Thumbs up on the corn fritters -- prepared very well and delicious. Not a fan of the Gado Gado because they combine cooked kale with cabbage, string beans and other veggies.

I tried Combo #2, which came with a huge bowl of either Chicken clear noodle soup or beef egg noodle soup (I chose the chicken);  3 skewers (2 chicken and for my 3rd I chose the beef potato), a small mound of rice. They were out of the perkedel meat patty so they asked me when I placed the order if they could give me another corn fritter as a substitute (I can't turn down fried corn :-)) Chicken sate skewers were very tender. Not too salty, but they provided a small dish of Indonesian soy in case I wanted to make it more savory. Beef and potato skewer was good too with a fresh sambal like red sauce.

Menu is not too large, but the have daily specials. I'm looking forward to coming back on Saturday when they offer the Nasi Kuning rice plate served on a banana leaf.

Cash or Credit card.

Parking lot with entrance on Palms -- they're 3 parking spots set aside for Mr. Sate customers.<//Text>

<Review>I tried their pork sate, chicken sate, fried rice, fried noodles (both mie goreng and mie tek tek), soto mie, soto Ayam, corn fritters, perkedel and balado bowl. The mie goreng contained too much shredded vegetables for a fried noodle dish. Mie tek tek was a better noodle dish.The satays, when done right, were delicious and juicy. Soto mie and soto ayam were good, but it needed more proteins. Corn fritters were oily and soggy. Perkedel was good, especially when you pair it with the balado bowl. My favorite was the balado bowl; it was sweet, spicy and delicious.

Service can be slow, but the staff is always so gracious. They always make me feel welcome.

Mr. Sate is definitely one of my favorite lunch spots.< /Review><pictures>None<//pictures><Response>None< /Response><GmapID>0x80c2bbccccc9b78d:0xecf3f0ff670a2d55<//GmapID></record>

< review>
Nice visit during off hours (of China Airlines flights) using Priority Pass, especially at lunch hour. Staff were attentive and polite, constantly keeping the lounge clean. Good selection of Anchor Beers, decent soup and sandwiches, plus modest assortment of fruit, brownies, other alcoholic beverages and bottled beverages. Uncrowded and tranquil compared with Air France/KLM lounge -- and that's the experience you want.< /review>

<Review>A time machine taking you back into a 1970s version of the Air France lounge that's a floor below. Dolly Parton videos and news videos on unauthorized Airbnb parties play atmospherically in the background of a cramped yet heavily furnished lounge. An American businessman frantically negotiates on the phone, punctuated by half-hearted attempts at Mandarian. Chills dumpling sit near pretzels and Chex-Mix. The bar is self serve, Asahi and Anchor Steam bringing intoxicating diversity.

You wonder how you got here as you down your third mini-wine spritzer. You wonder what they do with the paper sign-in forms. You sit in a relieving break from the bustle of the airport, an oasis of pleasant mediocrity. You leave and almost forget you were there, better for the experience but lost to the sands of time.<//Review>< Pictures>

<rating>1</rating><review>Beware of Gabriel Travel! They booked our flight on two separate tickets without informing us about it and it caused so much stress and almost led to $1,000 in lost flights.

Here's what happened.

1. MISINFORMATION. We were booking a flight to Russia. Our travel agent M. sent us a potential itinerary with a tight connection, which we were a bit concerned about, so we asked M. what would happen if any of our flights were delayed, and M. assured us that it would be okay, as it was the responsibility of the airline to rebook us on the next available flight. Satisfied with his answer, we spent an extra $200 to book the flight directly with him rather than doing it ourselves because we wanted the peace of mind that comes with a single-itinerary booking.

2. AGGRESSIVE BEHAVIOR. What a mistake trusting M would be. What happened later was this: the flight for the first part of the journey was delayed, and so we weren't going to make it to our final flight, which was under another itinerary and therefore NOT the responsibility of the airline to rebook. After I finally managed to reach M. to change the last flight, he was very aggressive as soon as I explained the situation. He interrupted me to explain "his side" and at one point I thought he would just hang up on me.

3. LYING. He claimed it was not his problem because he had warned us the flight was on two separate tickets. This is totally false. Both my mom and I were on the phone during the booking process, and at no point did he mention separate tickets to either of us. I've traveled to over 30 different countries and am a seasoned traveler, so I would NEVER have agreed to a booking of two separate tickets when one of the layovers was just 1 hour.

3. POOR JUDGMENT. When people book with travel agents, they rely on the agent to make good judgment calls about itineraries, and this did not happen here. In fact, M. should have done his research and he should never have even offered the itinerary he gave us. Here's why. The itinerary he created had a 1-hour connection in Amsterdam. If we didn't make it on that connection, a simple flight search shows that the next available flight would have been too late in the day for us to make it to the last leg of our trip. And while we didn't know this, he DID know that last leg was on a separate ticket. Essentially, $1,000 worth of tickets for the second part of the trip hinged on making that 1-hour layover. Would an experienced travel agent ever recommend a client such a risky ticket in the first place?

We called a few different travel agents and none could match the price Gabriel Travel did, and now we know why -- because M. gave us a very risky itinerary that the other agencies were too honest to offer. When I contacted the owner of the agency to explain the situation, he was apologetic about his employee's rude behavior and he discounted $60 off of our change fees. He listened carefully to the whole situation and followed up with me via phone. Unfortunately, he was not apologetic about the tickets, the stress it caused us, nor did he acknowledge his employee's incompetence. Instead, he claimed that we all experience stress in our lives and this is just something we have to deal with (and that it wasn't as bad as it could have been, eh?).

Don't make the same expensive mistake we did -- find a travel agent who makes smart, sound itineraries that you can trust so you can start and end your trip stress-free.<//review>< gmap_id>

< Text>
Think I just found my local go to spot for Mexican food.  According to wifey, this is a "Chilango" style food from CDMX. According to me it's just great food.

First off, everything here is super clean, super organized and freshly cooked to order.  ( Which, by the way, I feel is the only way to go about ordering food).  There's is outdoor seating, the ability to order outside the restaurant, asks ability to order inside as well.  Telenovelas is on the TV and the cook/chef/ owner is super cool and charismatic.

On to the food, we ordered a wet carne asada burrito (size of my forearm), an enchilada plate, quesadilla con pollo, 1 taco con papas, 1 taco con pollo, and 1 torta de carne. All for about $30 which I think is a pretty good price for the about of food we got and quality of the food.  Food was great, but for my taste the wet sauce for the carne asada was a bit salty, but other than that everything else was excellent!

Highly recommend Julianas because they're local, they're a small business and they're doing things right! Only reason it was a 4 star was because there were no prices on the menu because they're just added up on the spot.< /Text>

< text>
I rarely eat at Popeye's and it appears I'll be eating there even less now. My debit card and credit cards got demagnetized earlier this week and the new ones haven't arrived yet. I waited for 15 minutes in the drive-thru to be told they don't have the ability to enter the number manually. I don't know if the corporate higher ups don't want minimum wage employees to take on big tasks like punching in the digits on the card or if the teens of today aren't capable but it's disgraceful! I don't think it's the latter as the young man who helped me seemed up for the challenge and more than capable but when he asked the manager how to enter the numbers, the voice bellowing across the kitchen said, "We can't enter the numbers." Technology can't help this problem. This is a Popeye's issue. On the positive side, my $86 order was wasted as it got made but not paid for. I'd fix this if I owned a Popeye's. It seems like wasting food when people are hungry and customers time while not taking in a penny because of something businesses have been handling seamlessly for decades is a joke but it's not! I'm dead serious. Popeye's can't take demagnetized cards even if they're chipped. Since I know this is a problem I'll likely waste more of my time and place several orders a day using my demagnetized card so Popeye's goes bankrupt while employees eat the wasted food for free.<//text>

<Rate>4</Rate>< Text>
First time for this restaurant chain, due to my wife being tele-brain washed into wanting one of the chicken sandwiches they advertise. Went ahead  with her sandwich and also got the $10 deal (6 chicken pieces, two sides and 2 biscuits) and I ordered 6 more biscuits. I love biscuits so I had to do a comparison. Chicken was really good,  the entire family (3 of us) and we all agreed they would be seeing us again. Rated the biscuits as better than the fall apart ones at KFC and almost as good as some made at home with bisquick. We stayed with the mild for our first time,  but the rest of the family opted for the spicy the  next time. The store we visited was the closest to our home, which was about 6 miles away. On a positive note, the Sizzler which was part of our regular family dinning, and went out of business.....is currently slated to become a Popeyes. And it's only one mile from home. What a changing world we live in today.</Text>

<resp>None< /resp><Review>Standard Cajun fast food and offering drive through and delivery during coronavirus. Note that it took 50 minutes of waiting in the drive through line to get our food; there was one smart person who left the line and parked to pick up food. They were able to do that and get their food prior to us placing our order.

They skimped on the Cajun fries, which was disappointing. That being said, I was glad to finally have been able to try the much hyped spicy chicken sandwich. The sandwich is much bigger than the equivalent chickfila sandwich, but the spiciness comes from the sauce rather than the chicken itself. I liked how the chicken was breaded and it was still crunchy even after the 20 minute car ride home. < Review>
I really wanted to like this Popeye's as it is close to my house. The good news is that the food is delicious. It is my favorite takeout fried chicken and I really like their unique side dishes. The bad news is that while the people who help you are very nice, they don't seem to be very good at getting your order correct. My wife and I recently ordered the Tuesday special which is one leg and one thigh. We got three of them. When we got home, we found that we had one breast and one wing in all three orders. We wanted dark meat! On previous trips, we have ordered half mild and half spicy and received either all spicy or all mild. This last Tuesday, we went in to get the Tuesday special only to be told that they had temporarily stopped the Tuesday special because they keep running out of chicken. It's  Popeye's, they should never run out of chicken! It seems like poor management and poor training or maybe they just don't care. This is not rocket science! If you work at a chicken restaurant, you should be able to tell the difference between white and dark meat. I hope that they get their act together soon! I'm going to try the one in Glendora and hope it is better!< /Review>
